title="National Air Traffic Services">NATS</a><sup id="cite_ref-aip_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aip-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><br />Statistics from the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Aviation_Authority_(United_Kingdom)" title="Civil Aviation Authority (United Kingdom)">UK Civil Aviation Authority</a><sup id="cite_ref-stats_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>London Stansted Airport</b> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>STN</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>EGSS</b>) is an <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> located in <a href="/wiki/Stansted_Mountfitchet" title="Stansted Mountfitchet">Stansted Mountfitchet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Essex" title="Essex">Essex</a>, England, 42&#160;mi (68&#160;km) northeast of <a href="/wiki/Central_London" title="Central London">Central London</a>.\n</p><p>London Stansted serves over 160 destinations across Europe, Asia and Africa. Stansted is a base for a number of major European low-cost carriers, being the largest base for low-cost airline <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a>, with over 100 destinations served by the airline. In 2015, it was the <a href="/wiki/Busiest_airports_in_the_United_Kingdom_by_total_passenger_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="Busiest airports in the United Kingdom by total passenger traffic">fourth-busiest airport</a> in the United Kingdom after <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">Heathrow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">Gatwick</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester</a>. Stansted\'s runway is also used by private companies such as the <a href="/wiki/Harrods_Aviation" title="Harrods Aviation">Harrods Aviation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Titan_Airways" title="Titan Airways">Titan Airways</a>, and XJet terminals, which are private ground handlers that are able to handle private flights, charter flights, and state visits.\n</p><p>Converted to civil use from  <a href="/wiki/RAF_Stansted_Mountfitchet" title="RAF Stansted Mountfitchet">RAF Stansted Mountfitchet</a> in the late 1940s, Stansted was used by charter airlines. It came under British Airports Authority control in 1966. The privatised\n<a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport_Holdings" title="Heathrow Airport Holdings">BAA</a> sold Stansted in February 2013 to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airports_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Airports Group">Manchester Airports Group</a>  as a result of a March 2009 ruling by the <a href="/wiki/Competition_Commission" title="Competition Commission">Competition Commission</a> against BAA\'s monopoly position.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Stansted_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>London Stansted Airport has one main passenger terminal, near the village of <a href="/wiki/Stansted_Mountfitchet" title="Stansted Mountfitchet">Stansted Mountfitchet</a>. Three passenger satellites have departure gates; one is connected to the main terminal by an air bridge and the other two by the <a href="/wiki/Stansted_Airport_Transit_System" title="Stansted Airport Transit System">Stansted Airport Transit System</a> people mover.\n</p><p>The terminal building was designed by <a href="/wiki/Foster_and_Partners" title="Foster and Partners">Foster Associates</a> with input from structural engineer <a href="/wiki/Peter_Rice" title="Peter Rice">Peter Rice</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>  and features a "floating" roof, supported by a <a href="/wiki/Space_frame" title="Space frame">space frame</a> of inverted-pyramid roof trusses, creating the impression of a stylised swan in flight. The base of each truss structure is a "utility pillar", which provides indirect uplighting illumination and is the location for air-conditioning, water, telecommunications, and electrical outlets. The layout of the airport was originally designed to provide an unobstructed flow for passengers to arrive at the short-stay car park, move through the check-in hall, and go through security and on to the departure gates, all on the same level.\n</p><p>From 1997 to 2007, Stansted had rapid expansion of passenger numbers on the back of the boom in low-cost air travel, peaking at 24&#160;million passengers in the 12 months to October 2007, but passenger numbers declined in the next five years. Passenger totals later increased, and in 2016 recorded an annual increase of 8.0% to 24.3&#160;million, and numbers have since continued to rise.<sup id="cite_ref-stats_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Stansted_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Before_Stansted_Airport_aa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Before_Stansted_Airport_aa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Where Stansted Airport is now, as about 1935</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:B-26-stanst.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/B-26-stanst.jpg/220px-B-26-stanst.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="196" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="535" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:B-26-stanst.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Martin_B-26_Marauder" title="Martin B-26 Marauder">Martin B-26 Marauder</a> of the 344th Bomb Group at Stansted, 1944</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Avro_York" title="Avro York">Avro York</a> of the based <a href="/wiki/Air_Charter_Limited" title="Air Charter Limited">Air Charter Ltd</a> taking off on a trooping flight in 1955 with wartime hangars in the background</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_World_War">Second World War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Stansted_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Second World War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/RAF_Stansted_Mountfitchet" title="RAF Stansted Mountfitchet">RAF Stansted Mountfitchet</a></div>\n<p>The airfield opened in 1943 and was used during the Second World War as <a href="/wiki/RAF_Stansted_Mountfitchet" title="RAF Stansted Mountfitchet">RAF Stansted Mountfitchet</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Air_Forces" title="United States Army Air Forces">United States Army Air Forces</a> as a bomber airfield and as a major maintenance depot. Although the official name was Stansted Mountfitchet, the base was known as simply Stansted in both written and spoken form.\n</p><p>The station was first allocated to the <a href="/wiki/USAAF" class="mw-redirect" title="USAAF">USAAF</a> <a href="/wiki/Eighth_Air_Force" title="Eighth Air Force">Eighth Air Force</a> in August 1942 as a heavy-bomber airfield. As well as an operational bomber base, Stansted was also an <a href="/wiki/Air_Materiel_Command#Air_Technical_Services_Command" title="Air Materiel Command">Air Technical Services Command</a>  maintenance and supply depot concerned with major overhauls and modification of B-26s. After D-Day, these activities were transferred to France, but the base was still used as a supply storage area for the support of aircraft on the continent.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Postwar_use">Postwar use</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Stansted_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Postwar use">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>After the withdrawal of the Americans on 12 August 1945, Stansted was taken over by the <a href="/wiki/Air_Ministry" title="Air Ministry">Air Ministry</a> and used by No. 263 Maintenance Unit, RAF, for storage purposes. In addition, between March 1946 and August 1947, Stansted was used for housing German prisoners of war.<sup id="cite_ref-AIllfeb78_p70_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIllfeb78_p70-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 1946, the recently established British cargo airline, London Aero and Motor Services, equipped with ex-RAF <a href="/wiki/Handley_Page_Halifax" title="Handley Page Halifax">Handley Page Halifaxes</a>, moved into Stansted, using it as a base for its operations until it was wound up in July 1948.<sup id="cite_ref-AIllfeb78_p70-1_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIllfeb78_p70-1-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Ministry of Civil Aviation finally took control of Stansted in 1949 and the airport was then used as a base by several UK charter airlines. The US military returned in 1954 to extend the runway for a possible transfer to <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>. The transfer to NATO was never realised, however, and the airport continued in civil use, ending up under <a href="/wiki/BAA_Limited" class="mw-redirect" title="BAA Limited">BAA</a> control in 1966.\n</p><p>During the 1960s, \'70s, and early \'80s, the Fire Service Training School  was based on the eastern side of the airfield under the auspices of the Ministry of Transport and Civil Aviation, now the Civil Aviation Authority. The school was responsible for the training of all aviation fire crews for British airfields, as well as those of many overseas countries.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_operations">Commercial operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Stansted_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Commercial operations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:London_Stansted_Airport_main_entrance.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/London_Stansted_Airport_main_entrance.jpg/220px-London_Stansted_Airport_main_entrance.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/London_Stansted_Airport_main_entrance.jpg/330px-London_Stansted_Airport_main_entrance.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/London_Stansted_Airport_main_entrance.jpg/440px-London_Stansted_Airport_main_entrance.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:London_Stansted_Airport_main_entrance.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The terminal building at night</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:London_Stansted_Airport_-_Baggage_reclaim.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/London_Stansted_Airport_-_Baggage_reclaim.jpg/220px-London_Stansted_Airport_-_Baggage_reclaim.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/London_Stansted_Airport_-_Baggage_reclaim.jpg/330px-London_Stansted_Airport_-_Baggage_reclaim.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/London_Stansted_Airport_-_Baggage_reclaim.jpg/440px-London_Stansted_Airport_-_Baggage_reclaim.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2362" data-file-height="1764" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:London_Stansted_Airport_-_Baggage_reclaim.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The arrivals hall in the terminal building was extended in 2008.</div></div></div>\n<p>Beginning in 1966, after Stansted was placed under BAA control, the airport was used by holiday charter operators wishing to escape the higher costs associated with operating from Heathrow and Gatwick.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:London_Stansted_Airport_Air_View.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/London_Stansted_Airport_Air_View.jpg/220px-London_Stansted_Airport_Air_View.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/London_Stansted_Airport_Air_View.jpg/330px-London_Stansted_Airport_Air_View.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/London_Stansted_Airport_Air_View.jpg/440px-London_Stansted_Airport_Air_View.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1607" data-file-height="2143" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:London_Stansted_Airport_Air_View.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of Stansted from the air</div></div></div>\n<p>Stansted had been held in reserve as a third London airport since the 1950s. However, after a public inquiry at Chelmsford in 1966-67, the government set up the Roskill Commission to review the need afresh. The Commission for the Third London Airport (the "<a href="/wiki/Roskill_Commission" title="Roskill Commission">Roskill Commission</a>") of 1968-71 did not include Stansted as one of its four short-listed sites and recommended that <a href="/wiki/Cublington" title="Cublington">Cublington</a> in Buckinghamshire should be developed as London\'s third airport.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> However, the Conservative government under Ted Heath agreed with a minority recommendation that a site at Foulness in the Thames Estuary, later renamed Maplin, should be developed, but in 1974, the incoming Labour government under Harold Wilson cancelled the Maplin project because of the economic situation.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Stansted was then considered as an option for long-term development in the Advisory Committee on Airports Policy  and the Study Group on South East Airports  and was selected from a short list of six by the Conservative government in December 1979. The proposal, for a new terminal associated with the existing runway and the safeguarding of land for a second runway, was considered at the Airports Inquiries of 1981-83. The <i>Inspector\'s Report</i> was published in 1984 and the decision, announced in a white paper in 1985, was to approve a plan to develop Stansted in two phases, involving both airfield and terminal improvements that would increase the airport\'s capacity to 15&#160;million passengers per year, but to reject the second runway.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>The current terminal building was designed by architect <a href="/wiki/Norman_Foster,_Baron_Foster_of_Thames_Bank" title="Norman Foster, Baron Foster of Thames Bank">Norman Foster</a>. Construction was undertaken by <a href="/wiki/John_Laing_Group" title="John Laing Group">John Laing</a> and took place between 1988 and 1991,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> costing \xc2\xa3100&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In 1990, it was awarded the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Prize_for_Contemporary_Architecture" title="European Union Prize for Contemporary Architecture">European Union Prize for Contemporary Architecture / Mies van der Rohe Award</a>. As part of the development, a railway branch was built to the airport, and <a href="/wiki/Stansted_Airport_railway_station" title="Stansted Airport railway station">Stansted Airport railway station</a> opened in 1991.\n</p><p>Long-haul scheduled services commenced in the early 1990s when <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> operated a transatlantic service between Stansted and <a href="/wiki/O%27Hare_International_Airport" title="O&#39;Hare International Airport">O\'Hare International Airport</a>, but the route was unprofitable and was withdrawn in 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Continental_Airlines" title="Continental Airlines">Continental Airlines</a> also operated services in the late 1990s from <a href="/wiki/Newark_Liberty_International_Airport" title="Newark Liberty International Airport">Newark Liberty International Airport</a>, but this service was stopped shortly after the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a>.\n</p><p>Long-haul services to the United States returned in late 2005, when <a href="/wiki/Eos_Airlines" title="Eos Airlines">Eos Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/MAXjet_Airways" title="MAXjet Airways">MAXjet Airways</a> commenced all-business class services from Stansted to <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">New York\xe2\x80\x93JFK Airport</a>. In 2006, MAXjet expanded their service with flights to <a href="/wiki/Washington_Dulles_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Washington Dulles International Airport">Washington, DC</a>, <a href="/wiki/McCarran_International_Airport" title="McCarran International Airport">Las Vegas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_International_Airport" title="Los Angeles International Airport">Los Angeles</a>. American Airlines began daily flights to Stansted in October 2007 from New York\xe2\x80\x93JFK and was originally expected to operate a second daily flight from April 2008. However, because of the <a href="/wiki/2000s_energy_crisis" title="2000s energy crisis">jump in fuel price</a>, <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%932008" title="Financial crisis of 2007\xe2\x80\x932008">weakening economic performance</a>, and worsening credit environment at the time,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> all three services to the United States have since been discontinued following the demise of MAXjet Airways in December 2007 and Eos Airlines in April 2008. Finally, in July 2008, American Airlines withdrew from the airport.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Latest_developments">Latest developments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Stansted_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Latest developments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Long-haul transatlantic operations made a return to Stansted in June 2010, when <a href="/wiki/Sun_Country_Airlines" title="Sun Country Airlines">Sun Country Airlines</a> announced a seasonal weekly service from Stansted to <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis" title="Minneapolis">Minneapolis</a>. The flights made a refuelling stopover in <a href="/wiki/Gander_International_Airport" title="Gander International Airport">Gander</a>, Newfoundland, and Labrador as the aircraft used for the flight, a Boeing 737-800, would not be able to complete a nonstop westbound flight from Stansted to Minneapolis. The flights operated from 11 June to 15 August 2010. In 2011, Sun Country operated to Gatwick rather than Stansted and  then discontinued flights due to the price involved in carrying fuel on long-haul flights.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>.\nLong-haul services to Asia commenced in March 2009<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> with Malaysian low-cost airline <a href="/wiki/AirAsia_X" title="AirAsia X">AirAsia X</a> providing direct flights to <a href="/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur" title="Kuala Lumpur">Kuala Lumpur</a>; however, on 24 October 2011, this service moved to Gatwick Airport before being later withdrawn completely.\n</p><p>A major expansion programme to the existing terminal took place between 2007 and 2009, adding nearly 5,900&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (64,000&#160;sq&#160;ft) of floorspace to give space for additional baggage carousels, a new immigration and passport control hall, and a <a href="/wiki/Hypostyle" title="Hypostyle">hypostyle</a> arrivals hall with improved facilities.\n</p><p>In November 2006, <a href="/wiki/Uttlesford" title="Uttlesford">Uttlesford</a> District Council rejected a BAA planning application to increase the permitted number of aircraft movements and to remove the limit on passenger numbers. BAA immediately appealed against the decision and a public inquiry opened lasting from May until October 2007. Planning Inspector Alan Boyland made his recommendations in January 2008.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Those recommendations were largely followed by the Secretary of State for Transport (<a href="/wiki/Geoff_Hoon" title="Geoff Hoon">Geoff Hoon</a>) and the Secretary of State for Communities and Local Government (Hazel Blears), who jointly allowed the applicant\'s appeal in October 2008. A legal challenge by community campaign group Stop Stansted Expansion  was rejected by the High Court in March 2009. <sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2008, 57 people were arrested after <a href="/wiki/Plane_Stupid" title="Plane Stupid">Plane Stupid</a>, an environmental activist group, broke through the barriers and created a "stockade" on a taxiway, which resulted in 52 flights being cancelled.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Competition Commission ruled in March 2009 that BAA should sell Gatwick and Stansted Airports within two years.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The ruling was quashed within a year following an appeal, but was subsequently upheld.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The Competition Commission reconfirmed its ruling in July 2011 that the airport be sold,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Appeal_of_England_and_Wales" class="mw-redirect" title="Court of Appeal of England and Wales">Court of Appeal</a> turned down an appeal by BAA on 26 July 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> In light of the result, BAA chose not to appeal to the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Supreme Court of the United Kingdom">Supreme Court of the United Kingdom</a> and confirmed on 20 August 2012 that the airport would be sold.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2017, <a href="/wiki/Antonov_Airlines" title="Antonov Airlines">Antonov Airlines</a> opened a UK office at Stansted for cargo charter flights, generally of outsize loads.<sup id="cite_ref-aircargonews-20170220_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aircargonews-20170220-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Low-cost airline <a href="/wiki/Primera_Air" title="Primera Air">Primera Air</a> launched non-stop flights from Stansted to <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a> , <a href="/wiki/Newark_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Newark Airport">Newark</a> and <a href="/wiki/Washington_DC" class="mw-redirect" title="Washington DC">Washington DC</a> until the collapse of the airline meant the discontinuation of the routes by 2018, leaving the airport without transatlantic routes once more.\n</p><p>In March 2018, a group of activists delayed a deportation flight to Nigeria.<sup id="cite_ref-batchelor_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batchelor-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> 15 of the protestors were found guilty of "intentional disruption of services at an aerodrome", under the 1990 <a href="/wiki/Aviation_and_Maritime_Security_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Aviation and Maritime Security Act">Aviation and Maritime Security Act</a>. This verdict on the <i>Stansted 15</i> was described in <i><a href="/wiki/New_Statesman" title="New Statesman">New Statesman</a></i> as having a <a href="/wiki/Chilling_effect" title="Chilling effect">chilling effect</a> on public dissent.<sup id="cite_ref-camiss_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-camiss-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">easyJet</a> announced the closure of their base at Stansted, which had more than two dozen routes and existed for more than a decade, in August 2020,<sup id="cite_ref-easy_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-easy-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> followed by <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a>\' suspension of flights to <a href="/wiki/Dubai_International_Airport" title="Dubai International Airport">Dubai\xe2\x80\x93International</a> in September of the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Stansted_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_and_satellite_buildings">Terminal and satellite buildings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Stansted_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Terminal and satellite buildings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The terminal is separated into three areas: Check-in and main concourse along the front, Departures towards the back left, and Arrivals on the back right upon entry. No gates are in the main terminal building; instead, they are located in three separate oblong satellite buildings. \n</p><p>An additional building, known as the Advanced Passenger Vehicle (APV), was brought back into use in 2016 for flights departing during the busy 06:00 to 08:00 am period.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The APV building is linked to the main terminal building by an accessible route and acts as a bus terminal for international flights at remote stands. Prior to the completion of Satellite 3, this terminal (then consisted of gates 90-95) was in regular passenger use.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Satellite Building</th>\n<th>Gate Numbers</th>\n<th>Passenger access</th>\n<th>Notes\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Satellite 1</td>\n<td>1-19</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Stansted_Airport_Transit_System" title="Stansted Airport Transit System">Transit system</a></td>\n<td>Used by most airlines, except Ryanair, furthest in distance but first stop on transit from the main terminal. Around four minutes train ride.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td rowspan="2">Satellite 2\n</td>\n<td>20-39</td>\n<td>Transit system</td>\n<td>Used by Ryanair and Jet2. Situated in the upper level of Satellite 2 accessed via the second stop on transit from the main terminal. Boarding Bridges must be accessed by stairs one floor down (same level as gates 81-88). Around seven minutes train ride.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>81-88</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap">Walkway from main terminal</span></td>\n<td>Used for UK domestic flights but may be used for international departures; provides exit route for UK arrivals. During times of reduced operations, only gates 81-88 are used for boarding. Arriving passengers are transferred to Border Control via buses. (Below gates 20-39, and only takes up half of the first floor, but parallel to the bridges, which are also used by gates 20-39). Around ten minutes walk from the terminal.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Satellite 3</td>\n<td>40-59</td>\n<td>Walkway from main terminal</td>\n<td>Used exclusively by Ryanair; this building is not equipped with <a href="/wiki/Jet_bridge" title="Jet bridge">jet bridges</a>. Around fifteen minute walk from the main terminal.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>APV\n</td>\n<td>90-93\n</td>\n<td>Walkway from main terminal\n</td>\n<td>Used by Ryanair during peak times; acts as a terminal for buses to remote stands. The access to the gates is underneath the main terminal, next to the quiet zone. Around a four minute walk from the main passenger area.\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Domestic arrivals use a separate exit route, located at the opposite end of the Terminal to the International arrivals hall. This exit is connected solely by footbridge from Satellite 2 gates 81-88. When a domestic flight arrives at a gate which is not located in Satellite 2, passengers are transported to a gate on Satellite 2 by a courtesy bus service from the aircraft.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Car_parks_and_hotels">Car parks and hotels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Stansted_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Car parks and hotels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Radisson_Hotel_at_Stansted_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_321206.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Radisson_Hotel_at_Stansted_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_321206.jpg/220px-Radisson_Hotel_at_Stansted_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_321206.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="119" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Radisson_Hotel_at_Stansted_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_321206.jpg/330px-Radisson_Hotel_at_Stansted_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_321206.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Radisson_Hotel_at_Stansted_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_321206.jpg/440px-Radisson_Hotel_at_Stansted_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_321206.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="347" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Radisson_Hotel_at_Stansted_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_321206.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Radisson_Blu" title="Radisson Blu">Radisson Blu</a> hotel which is just a short walk from the Terminal building.</div></div></div>\n<p>Stansted has a variety of car parking including long-, mid-, and short-stay options along with valet and meet-and-greet parking services. Two drop off areas also are available. The express area is located near the short-stay car park, while a free service is within the mid-stay area. A fee is charged for the express service.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Terminal Road North and its free drop-off area directly outside the terminal was closed shortly after MAG took over the airport in 2013. Since 2004, Stansted also offers a range of hotel accommodation including <a href="/wiki/Holiday_Inn_Express" title="Holiday Inn Express">Holiday Inn Express</a>, <a href="/wiki/Novotel" title="Novotel">Novotel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Premier_Inn" title="Premier Inn">Premier Inn</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Radisson_Blu" title="Radisson Blu">Radisson Blu</a> hotels and the recently opened <a href="/wiki/Hampton_by_Hilton" title="Hampton by Hilton">Hampton by Hilton</a>, the last two of which are both within two minutes of the terminal building via an undercover walkway. Regular bus service handles transfers between the terminal building and Stansted\'s car parks and hotels.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Control_tower">Control tower</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Stansted_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Control tower">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stansted_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1761312.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Stansted_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1761312.jpg/220px-Stansted_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1761312.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Stansted_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1761312.jpg/330px-Stansted_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1761312.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Stansted_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1761312.jpg/440px-Stansted_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1761312.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="429" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stansted_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1761312.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Terminal Building with the adjacent Control Tower</div></div></div>\n<p>Stansted\'s <a href="/wiki/Air_traffic_control_tower" class="mw-redirect" title="Air traffic control tower">air traffic control tower</a> was completed in 1996 and was the tallest in Britain at the time of its construction.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> It is located on the southside of the airfield alongside the main terminal building. It replaced the old control tower, which offered poor views of the airfield once the current terminal building was opened in 1991.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_infrastructure">Other infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Stansted_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Other infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>There are several cargo buildings and hangars around the airfield. The main cargo centre is located by the control tower and handles most cargo operations, including aircraft such as the <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_MD-11" title="McDonnell Douglas MD-11">McDonnell Douglas MD-11</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747</a>. There are a small number of hangars on the other side of the runway to the rest of the airport. The largest are located at the south east of the airfield, one of which is used by Ryanair.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Titan_Airways" title="Titan Airways">Titan Airways</a> has its head office in the Enterprise House on the airport property.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Several airlines at one time had their head offices on the airport property. <a href="/wiki/AirUK" title="AirUK">AirUK</a> (later <a href="/wiki/KLM_uk" title="KLM uk">KLM uk</a>) had its head office in the Stansted House.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> When <a href="/wiki/Buzz_(airline)" title="Buzz (airline)">Buzz</a> existed, its head office was in the Endeavour House.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> When <a href="/wiki/AB_Airlines" title="AB Airlines">AB Airlines</a> existed, its head office was in the Enterprise House.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> For a period <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_International_Airways" title="Lloyd International Airways">Lloyd International Airways</a> had its head office at the Lloyd House at Stansted.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> When <a href="/wiki/Go_Fly" class="mw-redirect" title="Go Fly">Go Fly</a> existed its head office was at the Enterprise House.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Proposed_developments">Proposed developments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Stansted_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Proposed developments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Abandoned_plans_for_a_second_runway">Abandoned plans for a second runway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Stansted_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Abandoned plans for a second runway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 11 March 2008, BAA submitted a planning application (titled "G2") to expand the airport by 3&#160;sq&#160;mi (8&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) and for the construction of a second runway and terminal, etc., in line with a recommendation in the <a href="/wiki/Air_transport_and_the_environment_(United_Kingdom)#Airport_development_strategy" class="mw-redirect" title="Air transport and the environment (United Kingdom)">2003 Air Transport White Paper</a> (ATWP). This would have been the subject of a public inquiry, and if approved, would have allowed Stansted to handle more passengers than Heathrow did at the time of the application.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 2010, BAA withdrew its plans to build a second runway at Stansted and withdrew the plans to build a new runway at Heathrow.<sup id="cite_ref-withdraw_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-withdraw-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The ATWP had anticipated that a second runway would be operational by 2011, but this date continued to slip. BAA\'s 2008 planning application envisaged operation commencing in 2015, and in 2009, BAA revised the anticipated opening date to 2017.\n</p><p>Prior to the United Kingdom\'s May 2010 general election, all three major political parties pledged not to approve a second runway. Soon after the election, the new government confirmed this, and BAA withdrew its application for planning permission, having spent nearly \xc2\xa3200&#160;million preparing for the public inquiry and buying up properties.\n</p><p>The public inquiry into BAA\'s second runway application had been scheduled to start on 15 April 2009, but the start was delayed by Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Hazel_Blears" title="Hazel Blears">Hazel Blears</a> to allow time for BAA and the government to consider the implications of the March 2009 Competition Commission\'s ruling that BAA must sell Stansted within two years. As 2011 drew to a close, BAA was still appealing against the Competition Commission ruling. On 20 August 2012, after losing a case at the Court of Appeal, BAA agreed to cease challenging the Competition Commission\'s ruling and to sell Stansted.\n</p><p>On 10 February 2010, Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/John_Denham_(politician)" title="John Denham (politician)">John Denham</a>, in an open letter, concluded that the inquiry could not reasonably start until after the general election. In addition, he commented that the planning application documents were nearly two years old and would require updating. Eventually, BAA realised the futility of pursuing its G2 application in the context of the new government policy and withdrew it on 24 May 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-withdraw_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-withdraw-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Stop_Stansted_Expansion">Stop Stansted Expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Stansted_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Stop Stansted Expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Advocacy_group" title="Advocacy group">advocacy group</a> Stop Stansted Expansion (SSE) was formed in 2002, as a working group of the North West Essex and East Herts Preservation Association, in response to the Government\'s consultation on expanding UK airports and, particularly, expansion plans for Stansted Airport subsequently defined in the Air Transport white paper in December 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>SSE, whose membership includes the majority of local parish councils and thousands of residents, continues to actively campaign against unsustainable expansion of the airport. SSE was a major participant in the 2007 G1 public inquiry and had committed to be a major participant in the anticipated inquiry into the G2 second runway proposal. Following the withdrawal of the G2 planning application, the group called upon BAA to sell the homes it had bought to support the planned expansion.\n</p><p>In September 2012, as a result of pressure from the aviation industry, the government set up the Airports Commission, chaired by Sir Howard Davies,<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> to consider what, if anything, needed to be done to maintain the UK\'s status as a global aviation hub. The commission concluded that an additional runway would be required for South East England and that it should be added to either Heathrow or Gatwick. Following the 2015 election, the commission made a final recommendation to expand Heathrow subject to certain environmental constraints.\n</p><p>Throughout 2013, the Airports Commission published discussion papers and invited submissions from key stakeholders on the main issues it wished to consider. SSE made several thorough submissions. SSE also accepted an invitation to give oral evidence and make a presentation to the commission on aviation demand forecasting and connectivity at a public evidence session held in Manchester in July 2013.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_redevelopment">Terminal redevelopment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Stansted_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Terminal redevelopment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>MAG announced on 20 June 2013 as part of a visit to the airport by the Secretary of State for Transport that it would be launching an \xc2\xa380&#160;million terminal redevelopment programme. MAG has invested \xc2\xa340&#160;million and the remainder was invested by other commercial partners. The redevelopment included relocation of the security area, doubling the amount of seating, and improving the information displays. The new Departure Lounge offers a food court, a number of new shops, and an Escape Lounge, but the remodelling has drawn heavy criticism due to the length of time it takes to walk through the shopping areas to get to the departure gates.\n</p><p>Satellite One has also been redeveloped with the aim to attract more long-haul airlines to Stansted.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Arrivals_terminal">New Arrivals terminal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Stansted_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: New Arrivals terminal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>An arrivals terminal is planned to be built at Stansted, with construction due to begin in 2018, taking three years to complete. The site will include larger immigration and baggage reclaim areas, with more shops and facilities available after arrival into the UK. The current terminal will be reconfigured to departures only, with security and check-in areas due to be expanded. The project is expected to cost \xc2\xa3130m, and, once completed, will make London Stansted the only airport in the UK with dedicated arrivals and departures terminal buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Stansted_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Airlines and destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger">Passenger</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a Airport">Istanbul\xe2\x80\x93Atat\xc3\xbcrk</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistics">Statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Stansted_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Stansted_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1988, over 1.1&#160;million passengers passed through Stansted, the first time annual passenger numbers had exceeded 1 million at the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldstats_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldstats-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Consistent year-on-year growth followed, and by 1997, the total had reached over 5 million, rapidly rising to almost 12&#160;million in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-stats_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2007, passenger numbers peaked at nearly 24&#160;million, but then declined for five years, and in 2012, the total was around 17.5 million. An increase of 2.2% was recorded in 2013 to 17.8 million passengers, then 11.7% in 2014 to 19.9 million, followed by 12.8% in 2015 to 22.5&#160;million, and 8.0% in 2016 to a record total of 24.3&#160;million, making Stansted the <a href="/wiki/List_of_busiest_airports_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of busiest airports in the United Kingdom">fourth-busiest airport</a> in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-stats_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Stansted also is a major freight airport, the third-busiest in the UK during 2016, behind London Heathrow and East Midlands Airport, handling in excess of 223,203 tonnes per annum, although freight throughput has declined slightly from its 2005 peak level.<sup id="cite_ref-stats_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Passenger numbers for the year ending September 2016 increased by 8.4% to over 24&#160;million for the first time since 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traffic_figures">Traffic figures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Stansted_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Traffic figures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1017906329">@media all and (max-width:720px){body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol" title="Amsterdam Airport Schiphol">Amsterdam</a></td>\n<td align="right">358,127</td>\n<td><img alt="Increase" class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark"><img alt="Denmark" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Flag_of_Denmark.svg/20px-Flag_of_Denmark.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Porto Airport">Porto</a></td>\n<td align="right">322,504</td>\n<td><img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" class="mw-headline" id="Ground_transport">Ground transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Stansted_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Ground transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transit_system">Transit system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Stansted_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Transit system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stansted_Airport_People_Mover.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Stansted_Airport_People_Mover.JPG/220px-Stansted_Airport_People_Mover.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Stansted_Airport_People_Mover.JPG/330px-Stansted_Airport_People_Mover.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Stansted_Airport_People_Mover.JPG/440px-Stansted_Airport_People_Mover.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stansted_Airport_People_Mover.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The transit system which links the main terminal building to satellite buildings 1 (gates 1 \xe2\x80\x93 19) and 2 (gates 20 \xe2\x80\x93 39).</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Stansted_Airport_Transit_System" title="Stansted Airport Transit System">Stansted Airport Transit System</a></div>\n<p>The Stansted Airport Transit System connects the terminal to the satellite buildings via a 2&#160;mi (3&#160;km) free <a href="/wiki/Automated_people_mover" class="mw-redirect" title="Automated people mover">automated people mover</a> service, which runs on dual concrete tracks. The system uses a mix of <a href="/wiki/Adtranz_C-100" title="Adtranz C-100">Adtranz C-100</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Innovia_APM_100" title="Bombardier Innovia APM 100">Bombardier Innovia APM 100</a> vehicles to carry passengers to departure gates. Unlike the similar <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport_Shuttle_Transit" title="Gatwick Airport Shuttle Transit">Gatwick Airport Shuttle Transit</a>, the Stansted transit is only accessible "airside" (i.e. only after passengers pass through security).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trains">Trains</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Stansted_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Trains">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:379_027_Liverpool_St(8091065140).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/379_027_Liverpool_St%288091065140%29.jpg/220px-379_027_Liverpool_St%288091065140%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/379_027_Liverpool_St%288091065140%29.jpg/330px-379_027_Liverpool_St%288091065140%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/379_027_Liverpool_St%288091065140%29.jpg/440px-379_027_Liverpool_St%288091065140%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:379_027_Liverpool_St(8091065140).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Stansted_Express" title="Stansted Express">Stansted Express</a> at <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Street_station" title="Liverpool Street station">London Liverpool Street</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Stansted_Airport_railway_station" title="Stansted Airport railway station">Stansted Airport railway station</a> is situated in the terminal building directly below the main concourse.<sup id="cite_ref-officialaccess_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-officialaccess-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Services to London are on the <a href="/wiki/Stansted_Express" title="Stansted Express">Stansted Express</a> train to and from <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Street_station" title="Liverpool Street station">London Liverpool Street</a> in Central London. This service operates every 15 minutes and the usual journey time is roughly 45 to 53 minutes. Liverpool Street is served by the <a href="/wiki/Central_line_(London_Underground)" title="Central line (London Underground)">Central</a>, <a href="/wiki/Circle_line_(London_Underground)" title="Circle line (London Underground)">Circle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hammersmith_%26_City_line" title="Hammersmith &amp; City line">Hammersmith &amp; City</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_line" title="Metropolitan line">Metropolitan</a> lines of the <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">London Underground</a> network, offering access throughout London. The Stansted Express also calls at <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hale_station" title="Tottenham Hale station">Tottenham Hale</a>, for the Underground\'s <a href="/wiki/Victoria_line" title="Victoria line">Victoria line</a> and connections to various destinations in North London and the <a href="/wiki/West_End_of_London" title="West End of London">West End</a>. Some Stansted Express services also call at <a href="/wiki/Stansted_Mountfitchet_railway_station" title="Stansted Mountfitchet railway station">Stansted Mountfitchet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bishops_Stortford_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishops Stortford railway station">Bishop\'s Stortford</a>, and/or <a href="/wiki/Harlow_Town_railway_station" title="Harlow Town railway station">Harlow Town</a> en route to London Liverpool Street.<sup id="cite_ref-officialaccess_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-officialaccess-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/CrossCountry" title="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</a> operates three services from the airport to <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_New_Street_railway_station" title="Birmingham New Street railway station">Birmingham New Street</a>, via <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_railway_station" title="Cambridge railway station">Cambridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peterborough_railway_station" title="Peterborough railway station">Peterborough</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Leicester_railway_station" title="Leicester railway station">Leicester</a>. <a href="/wiki/Greater_Anglia_(train_operating_company)" title="Greater Anglia (train operating company)">Greater Anglia</a> operates services to <a href="/wiki/Norwich_railway_station" title="Norwich railway station">Norwich</a> via Cambridge.<sup id="cite_ref-officialaccess_77-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-officialaccess-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Buses_and_coaches">Buses and coaches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Stansted_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Buses and coaches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Scheduled express bus or coach services run to and from Stratford (45 minutes), <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Coach_Station" title="Victoria Coach Station">Victoria Coach Station</a> (75 minutes), <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Street_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Liverpool Street Station">Liverpool Street Station</a> (55 minutes), and <a href="/wiki/Portman_Square" title="Portman Square">Portman Square</a> via <a href="/wiki/Golders_Green" title="Golders Green">Golders Green</a> (70 minutes) and <a href="/wiki/Paddington_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Paddington Station">Paddington Station</a> (105 minutes) (all in London), costing about half the train fare, but taking longer. The bus station is next to the terminal building. <a href="/wiki/National_Express_Coaches" title="National Express Coaches">National Express</a> runs direct coach services to the airport from <a href="/wiki/Luton_Airport" title="Luton Airport">Luton Airport</a> and Heathrow, and also from Birmingham (11 a day), Oxford (8 a day), Norwich (10 a day), and Cambridge (11 a day).<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Stansted is also the start of the hourly X30 coach service to <a href="/wiki/Southend-on-Sea" title="Southend-on-Sea">Southend-on-Sea</a> via <a href="/wiki/Chelmsford" title="Chelmsford">Chelmsford</a> and <a href="/wiki/London_Southend_Airport" title="London Southend Airport">London Southend Airport</a> and the hourly X10 coach service to <a href="/wiki/Basildon" title="Basildon">Basildon</a> via Chelmsford, both operated by <a href="/wiki/First_Essex" title="First Essex">First Essex</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Local bus services operate to nearby communities, including the 510/509/508 (Harlow to Stansted via Stansted Mountfitchet, Parsonage Lane and Takeley, respectively), 7/7a (Bishops Stortford to Stansted), 133 (Braintree), and 6 (Saffron Walden), operated by Arriva. <sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">Roads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Stansted_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Roads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Stansted is connected to northeast London and Cambridge by the <a href="/wiki/M11_motorway" title="M11 motorway">M11 motorway</a> and to <a href="/wiki/Braintree,_Essex" title="Braintree, Essex">Braintree</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colchester" title="Colchester">Colchester</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Harwich" title="Harwich">Harwich</a> by the A120, which is dual-carriageway until Braintree. The road distance to London is 37 miles (60&#160;km).<sup id="cite_ref-officialaccess_77-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-officialaccess-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of October 1996, the airport has 2,500 short-stay parking spaces within walking distance to the terminal. In addition, as of the same month, the airport has over 8,000 long-stay spaces located near the M11 motorway and A120 junction. A courtesy bus service links the long-stay spaces to the terminal.<sup id="cite_ref-parking_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parking-82">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> The airport also offers mid-stay parking, closer to the terminal than its long-stay spaces.<sup id="cite_ref-parking_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parking-82">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Stansted Airport also offers valet parking and a meet-and-greet service, which is similar to valet, but marketed more at the leisure-traveller market, both are run from the short-stay car park.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Incidents_and_accidents">Incidents and accidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Stansted_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Incidents and accidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Stansted has been designated by the UK government as its preferred airport for any hijacked planes requesting to land in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> This is because its design allows a hijacked airliner to be isolated well away from any terminal buildings or runways, allowing the airport to continue to operate while negotiations are carried out, or even while an assault or rescue mission is undertaken. For this reason, Stansted has been involved in more hijack incidents than might be expected for an airport of its size.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>On 27 February 1982, an <a href="/wiki/Air_Tanzania" title="Air Tanzania">Air Tanzania</a> <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737" title="Boeing 737">Boeing 737-2R8C</a> landed at the airport after having been hijacked on an internal flight from <a href="/wiki/Mwanza_Airport" title="Mwanza Airport">Mwanza</a> to <a href="/wiki/Dar_Es_Salaam_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Dar Es Salaam Airport">Dar Es Salaam</a> and flown to the UK via Nairobi, Jeddah, and Athens, where two passengers had been released. The hijackers demanded to speak to exiled Tanzanian opposition politician <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Kambona" title="Oscar Kambona">Oscar Kambona</a>. This request was granted, and after 26 hours on the ground, the hijackers surrendered and the passengers were released.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcsth_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcsth-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 30 March 1998, an <a href="/wiki/Emerald_Airways" title="Emerald Airways">Emerald Airways</a> <a href="/wiki/Hawker_Siddeley_HS_748" title="Hawker Siddeley HS 748">Hawker Siddeley HS 748</a> carrying the <a href="/wiki/Leeds_United_F.C." title="Leeds United F.C.">Leeds United F.C.</a> was brought down immediately after takeoff when its starboard engine exploded. Forty passengers were onboard (18 from the Leeds team) and due to the quick thinking of the flight crew and the then Leeds assistant manager <a href="/wiki/David_O%27Leary" title="David O&#39;Leary">David O\'Leary</a>, only two people  came away with minor injuries.</li>\n<li>On 22 December 1999, <a href="/wiki/Korean_Air_Cargo_Flight_8509" title="Korean Air Cargo Flight 8509">Korean Air Cargo Flight 8509</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747-200F</a>, crashed shortly after take-off from the airfield due to pilot error. The only people on board at the time were the aircrew, and all four were killed. The aircraft crashed in <a href="/wiki/Hatfield_Forest" title="Hatfield Forest">Hatfield Forest</a> near the village of Great Hallingbury.</li>\n<li>On 6 February 2000, an <a href="/wiki/Ariana_Afghan_Airlines" title="Ariana Afghan Airlines">Ariana Afghan Airlines</a> <a href="/wiki/Boeing_727" title="Boeing 727">Boeing 727</a> with 156 people on board was hijacked and flown - stopping at Tashkent, Kazakhstan, and Moscow - to Stansted Airport. After a four-day stand-off, the hostages on board were safely freed and the incident ended peacefully. It later emerged that the motive behind the hijack was to gain asylum in the UK, sparking debate about immigration into the country. A large number of passengers on board the plane also applied for asylum. The remainder returned to Afghanistan.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Nine hijackers were jailed, but their convictions for hijacking were quashed for misdirection of the jury in 2003, and in July 2004, a court ruled that they could not be deported from the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 24 May 2013, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_International_Airlines" title="Pakistan International Airlines">Pakistan International Airlines</a> flight 709 from <a href="/wiki/Lahore,_Pakistan" class="mw-redirect" title="Lahore, Pakistan">Lahore, Pakistan</a>, was escorted by RAF Typhoons after being diverted from Manchester Airport due to an onboard threat. Two men were charged with endangering an aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 21 September 2013, <a href="/wiki/SriLankan_Airlines" title="SriLankan Airlines">SriLankan Airlines</a> flight UL503 inbound to Heathrow was escorted by RAF Typhoons to Stansted Airport after being diverted. Two men were detained for endangering an aircraft, one was formally arrested.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 4 October 2017, RAF Typhoons from the <a href="/wiki/Quick_Reaction_Alert" title="Quick Reaction Alert">Quick Reaction Alert</a> intercepted Ryanair flight FR2145 inbound to Luton and escorted it to Stansted Airport after a bomb threat. The threat was found to be a hoax.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Stansted_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_the_United_Kingdom_and_the_British_Crown_Dependencies" title="List of airports in the United Kingdom and the British Crown Dependencies">List of airports in the United Kingdom and the British Crown Dependencies</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Airports_of_London" title="Airports of London">Airports of
